<p><b>Novi Sad</b> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serbian_Cyrillic_language" title="Serbian Cyrillic language">Serbian Cyrillic</a>: <span lang="sr"><span class="Unicode">Нови Сад</span></span>, <small>pronounced </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Serbo-Croatian" title="Help:IPA for Serbo-Croatian">[nôʋiː sâːd]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata"> (<a href="/wiki/File:NoviSad.ogg" title="File:NoviSad.ogg"><img alt="" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="500" height="13" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/13px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/20px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/26px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 2x" width="13"/></a> <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/37/NoviSad.ogg" title="NoviSad.ogg">listen</a>)</small>; <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>: <span lang="hu"><i>Újvidék</i></span>; <a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">Slovak</a>: <span lang="sk"><i>Nový Sad</i></span>; see <a href="#Name">below</a> for other names) is the second largest <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Serbia" title="List of cities in Serbia">city</a> of Serbia, the capital of the autonomous province of <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a> and the administrative center of the <a href="/wiki/South_Ba%C4%8Dka_District" title="South Bačka District">South Bačka District</a>. It is located in the southern part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pannonian_Plain" title="Pannonian Plain">Pannonian Plain</a>, on the border of the <a href="/wiki/Ba%C4%8Dka" title="Bačka">Bačka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syrmia" title="Syrmia">Srem</a> geographical regions, on the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> river, facing the northern slopes of <a href="/wiki/Fru%C5%A1ka_Gora" title="Fruška Gora">Fruška Gora</a> mountain.</p>
<p>According to the 2011 census<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the city has a population of 250,439,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-media.popis2011.stat.rs_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-media.popis2011.stat.rs-2">[2]</a></sup> while the urban area of Novi Sad (with the adjacent urban settlements of <a href="/wiki/Petrovaradin" title="Petrovaradin">Petrovaradin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sremska_Kamenica" title="Sremska Kamenica">Sremska Kamenica</a>) has 277,522 inhabitants. The population of the administrative area of the city stands at 341,625 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Census_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-Census-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Novi Sad was founded in 1694, when <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serb" title="Serb">Serb</a> merchants formed a colony across the Danube from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petrovaradin_fortress" title="Petrovaradin fortress">Petrovaradin fortress</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habsburg" title="Habsburg">Habsburg</a> strategic military post. In the 18th and 19th centuries, it became an important trading and manufacturing centre, as well as a centre of <a href="/wiki/Serbian_culture" title="Serbian culture">Serbian culture</a> of that period, earning the nickname of the <i>Serbian Athens</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> The city was heavily devastated in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848_in_the_Habsburg_areas" title="Revolutions of 1848 in the Habsburg areas">1848 Revolution</a>, but it was subsequently restored. Today, along with the capital city of Belgrade, Novi Sad is the industrial and financial center of the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Serbia" title="Economy of Serbia">Serbian economy</a>; also, it was named one of the 2021 <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a> cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The name <i>Novi Sad</i> means "New Plant" (noun) in <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a>. Its Latin name, stemming from establishment of city rights, is "Neoplanta". The official names of Novi Sad used by the local administration are:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<table>
<tr>
<td>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Serbian_Cyrillic_alphabet" title="Serbian Cyrillic alphabet">Serbian Cyrillic</a>: <i>Нови Сад</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>: <i>Újvidék</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">Slovak</a>: <i>Nový Sad</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Rusyn_language" title="Pannonian Rusyn language">Rusyn</a>: <i>Нови Сад</i> (transliterated: <i>Novi Sad</i>)</li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In both <a href="/wiki/Croatian_language" title="Croatian language">Croatian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a>, which are official in the provincial administration, the city is called "Novi Sad". Historically, it was also called "Neusatz" in <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>.</p>
<p>In its wider meaning, the name <i>Grad Novi Sad</i> refers to the "City of Novi Sad", which is one of the city-level <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subdivisions_of_Serbia" title="Subdivisions of Serbia">administrative units</a> of <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>. <i>Novi Sad</i> could also refer strictly to the urban part of the City of Novi Sad (including "Novi Sad proper", and towns of <a href="/wiki/Sremska_Kamenica" title="Sremska Kamenica">Sremska Kamenica</a> and Petrovaradin), as well as only to the historical core on the left Danube bank, i.e. "Novi Sad proper" (excluding Sremska Kamenica and Petrovaradin).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Novi_Sad" title="History of Novi Sad">History of Novi Sad</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Older_settlements">Older settlements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Older settlements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Human dwelling on the territory of present-day Novi Sad has been traced as far back as the <a href="/wiki/Stone_Age" title="Stone Age">Stone Age</a> (about 4500 BC). Several settlements and <a href="/wiki/Necropolis" title="Necropolis">necropoleis</a> were unearthed during the construction of a new boulevard in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Avijaticarsko_Naselje" title="Avijaticarsko Naselje">Avijaticarsko Naselje</a>, and were dated to 5000 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> A settlement was located on the right bank of the river <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> in the territory of present-day <a href="/wiki/Petrovaradin" title="Petrovaradin">Petrovaradin</a>. In antiquity, the region was inhabited by <a href="/wiki/Illyrians" title="Illyrians">Illyrian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thracians" title="Thracians">Thracian</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Celtic_tribes" title="Celtic tribes">Celtic tribes</a>, especially by the <a href="/wiki/Scordisci" title="Scordisci">Scordisci</a>. Celts were present in the area since the 4th century BC and founded the first fortress on the right bank of the Danube. Later, in the 1st century BC, the region was conquered by the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a>. During Roman rule, a larger fortress was built in the 1st century with the name <i>Cusum</i> and was included in the <a href="/wiki/Roman_province" title="Roman province">Roman province</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pannonia" title="Pannonia">Pannonia</a>.</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">
<div style="width: 155px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">
<div style="margin:15px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Casque_orn%C3%A9_4%C3%A8me_si%C3%A8cle_Mus%C3%A9e_Novi_Sad_Colis%C3%A9e_Rome_Italie.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3018" data-file-width="2614" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Casque_orn%C3%A9_4%C3%A8me_si%C3%A8cle_Mus%C3%A9e_Novi_Sad_Colis%C3%A9e_Rome_Italie.jpg/104px-Casque_orn%C3%A9_4%C3%A8me_si%C3%A8cle_Mus%C3%A9e_Novi_Sad_Colis%C3%A9e_Rome_Italie.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Casque_orn%C3%A9_4%C3%A8me_si%C3%A8cle_Mus%C3%A9e_Novi_Sad_Colis%C3%A9e_Rome_Italie.jpg/156px-Casque_orn%C3%A9_4%C3%A8me_si%C3%A8cle_Mus%C3%A9e_Novi_Sad_Colis%C3%A9e_Rome_Italie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Casque_orn%C3%A9_4%C3%A8me_si%C3%A8cle_Mus%C3%A9e_Novi_Sad_Colis%C3%A9e_Rome_Italie.jpg/208px-Casque_orn%C3%A9_4%C3%A8me_si%C3%A8cle_Mus%C3%A9e_Novi_Sad_Colis%C3%A9e_Rome_Italie.jpg 2x" width="104"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><i>Roman Golden Helmet</i> , <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Vojvodina" title="Museum of Vojvodina">Museum of Vojvodina</a></p>
</div>

</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">
<div style="width: 155px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">
<div style="margin:32.5px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bredael_Schlacht_bei_Peterwardein.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="774" data-file-width="1089" height="85" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Bredael_Schlacht_bei_Peterwardein.jpg/120px-Bredael_Schlacht_bei_Peterwardein.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Bredael_Schlacht_bei_Peterwardein.jpg/180px-Bredael_Schlacht_bei_Peterwardein.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Bredael_Schlacht_bei_Peterwardein.jpg/240px-Bredael_Schlacht_bei_Peterwardein.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a></div>

</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">
<div style="width: 155px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">
<div style="margin:35px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Petrovaradin_after_1830.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1386" data-file-width="2085" height="80" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Petrovaradin_after_1830.jpg/120px-Petrovaradin_after_1830.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Petrovaradin_after_1830.jpg/180px-Petrovaradin_after_1830.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Petrovaradin_after_1830.jpg/240px-Petrovaradin_after_1830.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a></div>

</div>

</li>
</ul>
<p>In the 5th century, Cusum was devastated by the invasion of the <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">Huns</a>. By the end of the 5th century, <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantines</a> had reconstructed the town and called it by the names <i>Petrikon</i> or <i>Petrikov</i> (<a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el">Πετρικοβ</span>) after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Peter" title="St. Peter">St. Peter</a>. <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavic</a> tribes such as the <a href="/wiki/Severians" title="Severians">Severians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Obotrites" title="Obotrites">Obotrites</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">Serbs</a>, with its subgroup tribes <a href="/wiki/Brani%C4%8Devci" title="Braničevci">Braničevci</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timo%C4%8Dani" title="Timočani">Timočani</a>, settled today's region about Novi Sad mainly in the 6th and 7th centuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sava_S_1998.2C_page_36_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sava_S_1998.2C_page_36-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (April 2013)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>]</sup> The Serbs absorbed the aforementioned Slavs as well as the <a href="/wiki/Prehistory_of_Southeastern_Europe" title="Prehistory of Southeastern Europe">Paleo-Balkanic</a> peoples in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sava_S_1998.2C_page_36_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sava_S_1998.2C_page_36-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the Middle Ages, the area was subsequently controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Ostrogoths" title="Ostrogoths">Ostrogoths</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gepids" title="Gepids">Gepids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Avars" title="Pannonian Avars">Avars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Franks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_Moravia" title="Great Moravia">Great Moravia</a>, <a href="/wiki/First_Bulgarian_Empire" title="First Bulgarian Empire">Bulgaria</a>, again by Byzantines, and finally by the <a href="/wiki/Hungarians" title="Hungarians">Hungarians</a>. It was included into the medieval <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Kingdom of Hungary</a> between the 11th and 12th centuries. Hungarians began to settle in the area, which before that time was mostly populated by Slavs, and the place was mentioned first time under the Hungarian variant <i>Peturwarad</i> or <i>Pétervárad</i> (Serbian: <i>Petrovaradin</i> / Петроварадин), which derived from the Byzantine variant, in documents from 1237. In the same year, several other settlements were mentioned to exist in the territory of modern urban area of Novi Sad.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Novi_sad_19thcentury03_02.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1191" data-file-width="2367" height="111" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Novi_sad_19thcentury03_02.jpg/220px-Novi_sad_19thcentury03_02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Novi_sad_19thcentury03_02.jpg/330px-Novi_sad_19thcentury03_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Novi_sad_19thcentury03_02.jpg/440px-Novi_sad_19thcentury03_02.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Novi_sad_19thcentury03_02.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Novi Sad in 19th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From the 13th to 16th centuries, the following settlements existed in the territory of modern urban area of Novi Sad:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curcin_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Curcin-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Borovszky_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Borovszky-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>on the right bank of the Danube: <i>Pétervárad</i> (Serbian: <i>Petrovaradin</i>) and <i>Kamanc</i> (Serbian: <i>Kamenica</i>).</li>
<li>on the left bank of the Danube: <i>Baksa</i> or <i>Baksafalva</i> (<a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a>: <span lang="sr">Bakša, Bakšić</span>), <i>Kűszentmárton</i> (<a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a>: <span lang="sr">Sent Marton</span>), <i>Bivalyos</i> or <i>Bivalo</i> (<a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a>: <span lang="sr">Bivaljoš, Bivalo</span>), <i>Vásárosvárad</i> or <i>Várad</i> (<a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a>: <span lang="sr">Vašaroš Varad, Varadinci</span>), <i>Zajol I</i> (Serbian: <i><a href="/wiki/Gornje_Livade,_Novi_Sad" title="Gornje Livade, Novi Sad">Sajlovo I</a></i>, <i>Gornje Sajlovo</i>, <i>Gornje Isailovo</i>), <i>Zajol II</i> (Serbian: <i><a href="/wiki/Sajlovo" title="Sajlovo">Sajlovo II</a></i>, <i>Donje Sajlovo</i>, <i>Donje Isailovo</i>), <i>Bistritz</i> (Serbian: <i><a href="/wiki/Bistrica_(Novo_Naselje)" title="Bistrica (Novo Naselje)">Bistrica</a></i>).</li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tabula_hungariae.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4609" data-file-width="3236" height="242" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Tabula_hungariae.jpg/170px-Tabula_hungariae.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Tabula_hungariae.jpg/255px-Tabula_hungariae.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Tabula_hungariae.jpg/340px-Tabula_hungariae.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tabula_hungariae.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map from 1528 showing Petrovaradin (Peterwardein) and settlement named Bistrica (Bistritz) on the opposite side of Danube.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Some other settlements existed in the <a href="/wiki/Suburb" title="Suburb">suburban area</a> of Novi Sad: <i>Mortályos</i> (Serbian: <i>Mrtvaljoš</i>), <i>Csenei</i> (<a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a>: <span lang="sr"><a href="/wiki/%C4%8Cenej" title="Čenej">Čenej</a></span>), <i>Keménd</i> (Serbian: <i><a href="/wiki/Kamendin,_Sirig" title="Kamendin, Sirig">Kamendin</a></i>), <i>Rév</i> (<a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a>: <span lang="sr">Rivica</span>).</p>
<p>Etymology of the settlement names show that some of them are of <a href="/wiki/Slavic_languages" title="Slavic languages">Slavic</a> origin, which indicate that they were initially inhabited by Slavs. For example, Bivalo (Bivaljoš) was a large Slavic settlement dating to the 5th-6th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curcin_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-Curcin-9">[9]</a></sup> Some other settlement names are of <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a> origin (for example Bélakút, Kűszentmárton, Vásárosvárad, Rév), which indicate that they were inhabited by Hungarians before the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ottoman_invasion&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ottoman invasion (page does not exist)">Ottoman invasion</a> in the 16th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Borovszky_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Borovszky-10">[10]</a></sup> Some settlement names are of uncertain origin.</p>
<p>Tax records from 1522 showed a mix of Hungarian and Slavic names among inhabitants of these villages, including Slavic names like Bozso (Božo), Radovan, Radonya (Radonja), Ivo, etc. Following the Ottoman invasion in the 16th-17th centuries, some of these settlements were destroyed. Most surviving Hungarian inhabitants retreated from this area. Some of the settlements persisted during the Ottoman rule and were populated by ethnic Serbs.</p>
<p>Between 1526 and 1687, the region was under <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> rule. In the year 1590, population of all villages that existed in the territory of present-day Novi Sad numbered 105 houses, inhabited exclusively by Serbs. Ottoman records mention only those inhabitants who paid taxes, thus the number of Serbs who lived in the area (for example those that served in the <a href="/wiki/Military_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Military of the Ottoman Empire">Ottoman army</a>) was larger than that recorded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Founding_of_Novi_Sad">Founding of Novi Sad</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Founding of Novi Sad">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:23em; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 90%; background-color: #B0C4DE;">
<div class="" style="background-color: #B0C4DE; color: black; text-align: center; font-size: larger; font-weight: bold;">Historical affiliations</div>
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Flag_of_the_Habsburg_Monarchy.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Habsburg_Monarchy.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Flag_of_the_Habsburg_Monarchy.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Habsburg_Monarchy.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Flag_of_the_Habsburg_Monarchy.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_Habsburg_Monarchy.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></span> <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">Habsburg Monarchy</a> 1694-1804<br/>
<span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Flag_of_the_Habsburg_Monarchy.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Habsburg_Monarchy.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Flag_of_the_Habsburg_Monarchy.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Habsburg_Monarchy.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Flag_of_the_Habsburg_Monarchy.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_Habsburg_Monarchy.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Austrian_Empire" title="Austrian Empire">Austrian Empire</a> 1804-1867<br/>
<span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="432" data-file-width="648" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Flag_of_Austria-Hungary_%281869-1918%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Austria-Hungary_%281869-1918%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Flag_of_Austria-Hungary_%281869-1918%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Austria-Hungary_%281869-1918%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Flag_of_Austria-Hungary_%281869-1918%29.svg/45px-Flag_of_Austria-Hungary_%281869-1918%29.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></span> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_Empire" title="Austro-Hungarian Empire">Austro-Hungarian Empire</a> 1867–1918<br/>

<span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Flag_of_Hungary_%281915-1918%2C_1919-1946%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Hungary_%281915-1918%2C_1919-1946%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Flag_of_Hungary_%281915-1918%2C_1919-1946%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Hungary_%281915-1918%2C_1919-1946%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Flag_of_Hungary_%281915-1918%2C_1919-1946%29.svg/46px-Flag_of_Hungary_%281915-1918%2C_1919-1946%29.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></span> <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary_(1920%E2%80%9346)" title="Kingdom of Hungary (1920–46)">Kingdom of Hungary</a> 1941-1944<br/>
<span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="600" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Flag_of_SFR_Yugoslavia.svg/23px-Flag_of_SFR_Yugoslavia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Flag_of_SFR_Yugoslavia.svg/35px-Flag_of_SFR_Yugoslavia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Flag_of_SFR_Yugoslavia.svg/46px-Flag_of_SFR_Yugoslavia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">SFR Yugoslavia</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> 1944–1992<br/>
<span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="600" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Flag_of_Serbia_and_Montenegro.svg/23px-Flag_of_Serbia_and_Montenegro.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Flag_of_Serbia_and_Montenegro.svg/35px-Flag_of_Serbia_and_Montenegro.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Flag_of_Serbia_and_Montenegro.svg/46px-Flag_of_Serbia_and_Montenegro.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Serbia_and_Montenegro" title="Serbia and Montenegro">Serbia and Montenegro</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> 1992-2006<br/>
<span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1350" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Flag_of_Serbia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Serbia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Flag_of_Serbia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Serbia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Flag_of_Serbia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Serbia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> 2006-</p>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Habsburg rule was aligned with the Roman Catholic church and as it took over this area near the end of the 17th century, the government prohibited people of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church" title="Orthodox Church">Orthodox faith</a> from residing in <a href="/wiki/Petrovaradin" title="Petrovaradin">Petrovaradin</a>. Unable to build homes there, Serbs founded a new settlement in 1694 on the left bank of the Danube. They initially called it the "Serb city" (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <span lang="de"><i><a href="/wiki/Rascians" title="Rascians">Ratzen</a> Stadt</i></span>). Another name used for the settlement was Petrovaradinski Šanac. In 1718, the inhabitants of the village of <a href="/wiki/Alma%C5%A1" title="Almaš">Almaš</a> were resettled to Petrovaradinski Šanac, where they founded <a href="/wiki/Alma%C5%A1ki_Kraj" title="Almaški Kraj">Almaški Kraj</a> ("the Almaš quarter").</p>
<p>According to 1720 data, the population of Ratzen Stadt was composed of 112 Serbian, 14 German, and 5 Hungarian houses. The settlement officially gained the present names <i>Novi Sad</i> and <i>Újvidék</i> (<i>Neoplanta</i> in Latin) in 1748 when it became a "free royal city".</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%C3%9Ajvid%C3%A9k_V%C3%A1rosh%C3%A1za_1900.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="897" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/%C3%9Ajvid%C3%A9k_V%C3%A1rosh%C3%A1za_1900.jpg/220px-%C3%9Ajvid%C3%A9k_V%C3%A1rosh%C3%A1za_1900.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/%C3%9Ajvid%C3%A9k_V%C3%A1rosh%C3%A1za_1900.jpg/330px-%C3%9Ajvid%C3%A9k_V%C3%A1rosh%C3%A1za_1900.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/%C3%9Ajvid%C3%A9k_V%C3%A1rosh%C3%A1za_1900.jpg/440px-%C3%9Ajvid%C3%A9k_V%C3%A1rosh%C3%A1za_1900.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%C3%9Ajvid%C3%A9k_V%C3%A1rosh%C3%A1za_1900.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Novi Sad main square, 1900</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The edict that made Novi Sad a "free royal city" was proclaimed on 1 February 1748. The edict reads:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p><i>" We, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maria_Theresa_of_Austria" title="Maria Theresa of Austria">Maria Theresa</a>, by the grace of God <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empress" title="Holy Roman Empress">Holy Roman Empress</a>,<br/>
Queen of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moravia" title="Moravia">Moravia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dalmatia" title="Dalmatia">Dalmatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slavonia" title="Slavonia">Slavonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prozor-Rama" title="Prozor-Rama">Rama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galicia_(Central-Eastern_Europe)" title="Galicia (Central-Eastern Europe)">Galicia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lodomeria" title="Lodomeria">Lodomeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Carinthia" title="Duchy of Carinthia">Carinthia</a>, [...]<br/>
cast this proclamation to anyone, whom it might concern... so that the renowned Petrovaradinski Šanac, which lies on the other side of the Danube in the <a href="/wiki/Ba%C4%8Dka" title="Bačka">Bačka</a> province on the <a href="/wiki/Sajlovo" title="Sajlovo">Sajlovo</a> land, by the might of our divine royal power and prestige...make this town a <a href="/wiki/Free_imperial_city" title="Free imperial city">Free Royal City</a> and to fortify, accept and acknowledge it as one of the free royal cities of our <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Kingdom of Hungary</a> and other territories, by abolishing its previous name of Petrovaradinski Šanac, renaming it Neoplantae (<a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a>), Új-Vidégh (<a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>), Neusatz (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>) and Novi Sad (<a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a>) "</i>.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>In the 18th century, the Habsburg monarchy also recruited Germans from the southern principalities to relocate to the Danube valley. They wanted both to increase the population and to redevelop the river valley for agriculture, which had declined markedly under the Ottomans. To encourage such settlement, the government agreed that the German communities could practice their religion (mostly Catholicism) and use their original German dialect.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Habsburg_Monarchy_and_Austria-Hungary">Habsburg Monarchy and Austria-Hungary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Habsburg Monarchy and Austria-Hungary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>For much of the 18th and 19th centuries, Novi Sad was the largest Serb-inhabited city in the world; reformer of the Serbian language, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vuk_Stefanovi%C4%87_Karad%C5%BEi%C4%87" title="Vuk Stefanović Karadžić">Vuk Stefanović Karadžić</a>, wrote in 1817 that Novi Sad was the "largest Serb municipality in the world". It was a cultural and political centre of Serbs (see also <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Revival" title="Serbian Revival">Serbian Revival</a>), who did not have their own <a href="/wiki/Nation_state" title="Nation state">national state</a> at the time. Because of its cultural and political influence, Novi Sad became known as the "Serbian <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>" (<i>Srpska Atina</i> in Serbian). According to 1843 data, Novi Sad had 17,332 inhabitants, of whom 9,675 were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church" title="Orthodox Church">Orthodox Christians</a>, 5,724 <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholics</a>, 1,032 <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestants</a>, 727 <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>, and 30 adherents of the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Apostolic_Church" title="Armenian Apostolic Church">Armenian church</a>. The largest <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic group</a> in the city were Serbs, and the second largest were <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">Germans</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Velika-narodna-skupstina-1918.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1101" data-file-width="2006" height="121" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Velika-narodna-skupstina-1918.jpg/220px-Velika-narodna-skupstina-1918.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Velika-narodna-skupstina-1918.jpg/330px-Velika-narodna-skupstina-1918.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Velika-narodna-skupstina-1918.jpg/440px-Velika-narodna-skupstina-1918.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Velika-narodna-skupstina-1918.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Great People's Assembly of Banat, Bačka and Baranja, held in Novi Sad in November 25, 1918. proclaimed joining of Banat, Bačka and Baranja to the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia" title="Kingdom of Serbia">Kingdom of Serbia</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848" title="Revolutions of 1848">Revolution of 1848-1849</a>, Novi Sad was part of <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Vojvodina" title="Serbian Vojvodina">Serbian Vojvodina</a>, a Serbian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autonomous_area" title="Autonomous area">autonomous region</a> within the Austrian Empire. In 1849, the Hungarian garrison located on the Petrovaradin Fortress bombarded and devastated the city, which lost much of its population. According to an 1850 census, there were only 7,182 citizens in the city, compared with 17,332 in 1843. Between 1849 and 1860, the city was part of a separate Austrian crownland known as the <a href="/wiki/Voivodeship_of_Serbia_and_Banat_of_Temeschwar" title="Voivodeship of Serbia and Banat of Temeschwar">Voivodeship of Serbia and Banat of Temeschwar</a>. After the abolishment of this province, the city was included into <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A1cs-Bodrog_County" title="Bács-Bodrog County">Batsch-Bodrog</a> County. The post-office was opened in 1853.</p>
<p>After the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Compromise_of_1867" title="Compromise of 1867">compromise of 1867</a>, Novi Sad was located within the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Kingdom of Hungary</a>, the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transleithania" title="Transleithania">Transleithania</a></i>, one of two parts of <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a>. During this time, the <a href="/wiki/Magyarization" title="Magyarization">Magyarization</a> policy of the Hungarian government drastically altered the demographic structure of the city, i.e. from the predominantly Serbian, the population of the city became ethnically mixed. In 1880 41.2% of the city's inhabitants used <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian language</a> most frequently and 25.9% used Hungarian. In the following decades, percentual participation of Serbian-speakers decreased, while Hungarian-speakers increased. According to the 1910 census, the city had 33,590 residents, of whom 13,343 (39.72%) spoke Hungarian, 11,594 (34.52%) Serbian, 5,918 (17.62%) German and 1,453 (4.33%) Slovak. It is not certain whether Hungarians or Serbs were the larger ethnic group in the city in 1910, since the various ethnic groups (<a href="/wiki/Bunjevci" title="Bunjevci">Bunjevci</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>, other <a href="/wiki/South_Slavs" title="South Slavs">South Slavic</a> people, etc.) were classified in census results according to the language they spoke.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Similar demographic change can be seen in the religious structure: in 1870, population of Novi Sad included 8,134 Orthodox Christians, 6,684 Catholics, 1,725 Calvinists, 1,343 Lutherans, and others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> In 1910, the population included 13,383 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholics" title="Roman Catholics">Roman Catholics</a> and 11,553 <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Orthodox Christians</a>, while 3,089 declared themselves as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lutheran" title="Lutheran">Lutheran</a>, 2,751 as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Calvinist" title="Calvinist">Calvinist</a>, and 2,326 as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish" title="Jewish">Jewish</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Yugoslavia_and_Serbia">Yugoslavia and Serbia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Yugoslavia and Serbia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 25 November 1918, the <i>Assembly of Serbs, Bunjevci and other Slavs of Vojvodina</i> in Novi Sad proclaimed the union of Vojvodina region with the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia" title="Kingdom of Serbia">Kingdom of Serbia</a>. Since 1 December 1918, Novi Sad was part of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Kingdom of Serbs, Croats, and Slovenes</a>; and in 1929, it became the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Danube_Banovina" title="Danube Banovina">Danube Banovina</a>, a province of the Kingdom of Yugoslavia. In 1921, population of Novi Sad numbered 39,122 inhabitants, of whom 16,293 spoke Serbian language, 12,991 Hungarian, 6,373 German, 1,117 Slovak, etc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:328px;max-width:328px">

</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%C3%9Ajvid%C3%A9k_bomb%C3%A1z%C3%A1sa_a_II._vil%C3%A1gh%C3%A1bor%C3%BA_alatt._Fortepan_15956.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2813" data-file-width="3719" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/%C3%9Ajvid%C3%A9k_bomb%C3%A1z%C3%A1sa_a_II._vil%C3%A1gh%C3%A1bor%C3%BA_alatt._Fortepan_15956.jpg/150px-%C3%9Ajvid%C3%A9k_bomb%C3%A1z%C3%A1sa_a_II._vil%C3%A1gh%C3%A1bor%C3%BA_alatt._Fortepan_15956.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/%C3%9Ajvid%C3%A9k_bomb%C3%A1z%C3%A1sa_a_II._vil%C3%A1gh%C3%A1bor%C3%BA_alatt._Fortepan_15956.jpg/225px-%C3%9Ajvid%C3%A9k_bomb%C3%A1z%C3%A1sa_a_II._vil%C3%A1gh%C3%A1bor%C3%BA_alatt._Fortepan_15956.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/%C3%9Ajvid%C3%A9k_bomb%C3%A1z%C3%A1sa_a_II._vil%C3%A1gh%C3%A1bor%C3%BA_alatt._Fortepan_15956.jpg/300px-%C3%9Ajvid%C3%A9k_bomb%C3%A1z%C3%A1sa_a_II._vil%C3%A1gh%C3%A1bor%C3%BA_alatt._Fortepan_15956.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent"><b>Left:</b> <a href="/wiki/Novi_Sad_raid" title="Novi Sad raid">Novi Sad raid</a>, series of attacks by Hungarian troops against civilians in <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_occupation_of_Yugoslav_territories" title="Hungarian occupation of Yugoslav territories">Hungarian occupied Bačka</a> 1942.<br/>
<b>Right:</b><a href="/wiki/History_of_Novi_Sad" title="History of Novi Sad">Bombing of Novi Sad in WW2</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1941, Yugoslavia was invaded and partitioned by the <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis powers</a>, and its northern parts, including Novi Sad, were annexed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hungary_during_World_War_II" title="Hungary during World War II">Hungary</a>. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, about 5,000 citizens were murdered and many others were resettled. In three days of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1942_raid_in_Novi_Sad" title="1942 raid in Novi Sad">Novi Sad raid</a> (21–23 January 1942) alone, Hungarian police killed 1,246 citizens, among them more than 800 Jews, and threw their corpses into the icy waters of the Danube.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kil%C3%A1t%C3%A1s_a_P%C3%A9terv%C3%A1radi_er%C5%91db%C5%91l_a_V%C3%A1radi_h%C3%ADd_pill%C3%A9reire_%C3%A9s_a_h%C3%ADdf%C5%91_romjaira._Fortepan_16181.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3790" data-file-width="2808" height="229" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Kil%C3%A1t%C3%A1s_a_P%C3%A9terv%C3%A1radi_er%C5%91db%C5%91l_a_V%C3%A1radi_h%C3%ADd_pill%C3%A9reire_%C3%A9s_a_h%C3%ADdf%C5%91_romjaira._Fortepan_16181.jpg/170px-Kil%C3%A1t%C3%A1s_a_P%C3%A9terv%C3%A1radi_er%C5%91db%C5%91l_a_V%C3%A1radi_h%C3%ADd_pill%C3%A9reire_%C3%A9s_a_h%C3%ADdf%C5%91_romjaira._Fortepan_16181.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Kil%C3%A1t%C3%A1s_a_P%C3%A9terv%C3%A1radi_er%C5%91db%C5%91l_a_V%C3%A1radi_h%C3%ADd_pill%C3%A9reire_%C3%A9s_a_h%C3%ADdf%C5%91_romjaira._Fortepan_16181.jpg/255px-Kil%C3%A1t%C3%A1s_a_P%C3%A9terv%C3%A1radi_er%C5%91db%C5%91l_a_V%C3%A1radi_h%C3%ADd_pill%C3%A9reire_%C3%A9s_a_h%C3%ADdf%C5%91_romjaira._Fortepan_16181.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Kil%C3%A1t%C3%A1s_a_P%C3%A9terv%C3%A1radi_er%C5%91db%C5%91l_a_V%C3%A1radi_h%C3%ADd_pill%C3%A9reire_%C3%A9s_a_h%C3%ADdf%C5%91_romjaira._Fortepan_16181.jpg/340px-Kil%C3%A1t%C3%A1s_a_P%C3%A9terv%C3%A1radi_er%C5%91db%C5%91l_a_V%C3%A1radi_h%C3%ADd_pill%C3%A9reire_%C3%A9s_a_h%C3%ADdf%C5%91_romjaira._Fortepan_16181.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kil%C3%A1t%C3%A1s_a_P%C3%A9terv%C3%A1radi_er%C5%91db%C5%91l_a_V%C3%A1radi_h%C3%ADd_pill%C3%A9reire_%C3%A9s_a_h%C3%ADdf%C5%91_romjaira._Fortepan_16181.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Prince Tomislav Karađorđević Bridge destroyed in <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The total death toll of the raid was around 2,500.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cesarani_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cesarani-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sajti_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sajti-20">[20]</a></sup> Citizens of all nationalities—Serbs, Hungarians, Slovaks, and others—fought together against the Axis authorities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sajti_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sajti-20">[20]</a></sup> In 1975 the whole city was awarded the title <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_People%27s_Hero" title="Order of the People's Hero">People's Hero of Yugoslavia</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Partisans" title="Yugoslav Partisans">Yugoslav Partisans</a> from <a href="/wiki/Syrmia" title="Syrmia">Syrmia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ba%C4%8Dka" title="Bačka">Bačka</a> entered the city on 23 October 1944. During the Military administration in <a href="/wiki/Banat,_Ba%C4%8Dka_and_Baranja" title="Banat, Bačka and Baranja">Banat, Bačka and Baranja</a> (October 17, 1944 – January 27, 1945), the Partisans <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1944%E2%80%931945_killings_in_Vojvodina" title="1944–1945 killings in Vojvodina">killed a number of citizens</a>, mostly Serbs, who were perceived as opponents to the new regime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (June 2016)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Novi Sad became part of the new <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a>. Since 1945, Novi Sad has been the capital of <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Autonomous_Province_of_Vojvodina" title="Socialist Autonomous Province of Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a>, a province of the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Serbia" title="Socialist Republic of Serbia">Republic of Serbia</a>. The city went through rapid industrialization and its population more than doubled in the period between World War II and the breakup of Yugoslavia after the fall of the Soviet Union.</p>
<p>After 1992, Novi Sad was part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a>. Devastated by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1999_NATO_bombing_of_Yugoslavia" title="1999 NATO bombing of Yugoslavia">NATO bombardment</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">Kosovo War</a> of 1999, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1999_NATO_bombing_of_Novi_Sad" title="1999 NATO bombing of Novi Sad">Novi Sad was left</a> without any of its three Danube bridges, communications, water, and electricity. Residential areas were cluster-bombed several times while its <a href="/wiki/Oil_refinery" title="Oil refinery">oil refinery</a> was bombarded daily, causing severe pollution and widespread ecological damage. In 2003 FR Yugoslavia transformed into the <a href="/wiki/Political_union" title="Political union">state union</a> of <a href="/wiki/Serbia_and_Montenegro" title="Serbia and Montenegro">Serbia and Montenegro</a>, while Serbia became independent in 2006 (following <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Montenegrin_independence" title="Montenegrin independence">Montenegrin independence</a>).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The city lies on the S-shaped meander of the river Danube, which is only 350 meters wide beneath the Petrovaradin rock.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GeoNS_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-GeoNS-22">[22]</a></sup> A section of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Danube-Tisa-Danube_Canal" title="Danube-Tisa-Danube Canal">Danube-Tisa-Danube Canal</a> marks the northern edge of wider city centre, and merges with the Danube. The main part of the city lies on the left bank of the Danube, in <a href="/wiki/Ba%C4%8Dka" title="Bačka">Bačka</a> region, while smaller parts <a href="/wiki/Petrovaradin" title="Petrovaradin">Petrovaradin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sremska_Kamenica" title="Sremska Kamenica">Sremska Kamenica</a> lie on the right bank, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Srem" title="Srem">Srem</a> (Syrmia) region. Bačka side of the city lies on one of the southern lowest parts of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pannonian_Plain" title="Pannonian Plain">Pannonian Plain</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Fru%C5%A1ka_Gora" title="Fruška Gora">Fruška Gora</a> side (Syrmia) is a <a href="/wiki/Horst_(geology)" title="Horst (geology)">horst</a> mountain. <a href="/wiki/Alluvial_plain" title="Alluvial plain">Alluvial plains</a> along Danube are well-formed, especially on the left bank, in some parts 10 kilometres (6 miles) from the river. A large part of Novi Sad lies on a <a href="/wiki/Fluvial_terrace" title="Fluvial terrace">fluvial terrace</a> with an <a href="/wiki/Elevation" title="Elevation">elevation</a> of 80 to 83 metres (262 to 272 feet). The northern part of Fruška Gora is composed of massive <a href="/wiki/Landslide" title="Landslide">landslide</a> zones, but they are not active, except in the <a href="/wiki/Ribnjak,_Novi_Sad" title="Ribnjak, Novi Sad">Ribnjak</a> neighborhood (between <a href="/wiki/Sremska_Kamenica" title="Sremska Kamenica">Sremska Kamenica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Petrovaradin_Fortress" title="Petrovaradin Fortress">Petrovaradin Fortress</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UrbNS_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-UrbNS-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:1008px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Novi_Sad_-_Gigapixelna_panorama2.jpg" title="Panoramic view of Novi Sad from Petrovaradin Fortress"><img alt="" data-file-height="324" data-file-width="1800" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Novi_Sad_-_Gigapixelna_panorama2.jpg/1000px-Novi_Sad_-_Gigapixelna_panorama2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Novi_Sad_-_Gigapixelna_panorama2.jpg/1500px-Novi_Sad_-_Gigapixelna_panorama2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/55/Novi_Sad_-_Gigapixelna_panorama2.jpg 2x" width="1000"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Novi_Sad_-_Gigapixelna_panorama2.jpg" title="File:Novi Sad - Gigapixelna panorama2.jpg"></a></div>
Panoramic view of Novi Sad from <a href="/wiki/Petrovaradin_Fortress" title="Petrovaradin Fortress">Petrovaradin Fortress</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The total land area of the city is 699 square kilometres (270 sq mi), while the urban area is 129.7 km<sup>2</sup> (50 sq mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GeoNS_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-GeoNS-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Novi Sad has a temperate <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental climate</a>, with four seasons. Autumn is longer than spring, with long sunny and warm periods. Winter is not so severe, with an average of 22 days of complete sub-zero temperature, and averages 25 days of snowfall. January is the coldest month, with an average temperature of −1.9 °C (28.6 °F). Spring is usually short and rainy, while summer arrives abruptly. The coldest temperature ever recorded in Novi Sad was −30.7 °C (−23.3 °F) on 24 January 1963; and the hottest temperature ever recorded was 41.6 °C (106.9 °F) on 24 July 2007.</p>
<p>The east-southeasterly wind <a href="/wiki/Ko%C5%A1ava_(wind)" title="Košava (wind)">Košava</a>, which blows from the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">Carpathians</a> and brings clear and dry weather, is characteristic of the local climate. It mostly blows in autumn and winter, in 2–3 days intervals. The <a href="/wiki/Velocity" title="Velocity">average speed</a> of Košava is 25 to 43 km (16 to 27 mi) per hour but certain strokes can reach up to 130 km/h (81 mph). In winter time, accompanied by <a href="/wiki/Winter_storm" title="Winter storm">snow storms</a>, it can cause snowdrifts.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape">Cityscape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Cityscape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Famous_buildings_in_Novi_Sad" title="Famous buildings in Novi Sad">Famous buildings in Novi Sad</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:393px;max-width:393px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Palata_Menrat.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Palata_Menrat.JPG/180px-Palata_Menrat.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Palata_Menrat.JPG/270px-Palata_Menrat.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Palata_Menrat.JPG/360px-Palata_Menrat.JPG 2x" width="180"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:207px;max-width:207px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Serbia-0271_-_Pedestrian_Street_(7344452054).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Serbia-0271_-_Pedestrian_Street_%287344452054%29.jpg/205px-Serbia-0271_-_Pedestrian_Street_%287344452054%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Serbia-0271_-_Pedestrian_Street_%287344452054%29.jpg/308px-Serbia-0271_-_Pedestrian_Street_%287344452054%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Serbia-0271_-_Pedestrian_Street_%287344452054%29.jpg/410px-Serbia-0271_-_Pedestrian_Street_%287344452054%29.jpg 2x" width="205"/></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent"><b>Left:</b> Menrat Palace<br/>
<b>Right:</b>Zmaj Jovina street</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Novi Sad is a typical <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central European</a> town. There are only a few buildings dating before 19th century, because the city was almost totally destroyed during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848_in_the_Habsburg_areas" title="Revolutions of 1848 in the Habsburg areas">1848/1849 revolution</a>, so the architecture from 19th century dominates the <a href="/wiki/Stari_Grad,_Novi_Sad" title="Stari Grad, Novi Sad">city centre</a>. Around the center, old small houses used to dominate the cityscape, but they are being replaced by modern multi-story buildings.</p>
<p>During the socialist period, new blocks with wide streets and multi-story buildings were built around the city core. However, not many <a href="/wiki/Plattenbau" title="Plattenbau">communist-style</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High-rise" title="High-rise">high-rise</a> buildings were built, and the total number of 10+ floor buildings remained at 40-50, most of the rest being 3-6 floor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apartment_building" title="Apartment building">apartment buildings</a>. City's new <a href="/wiki/Boulevard" title="Boulevard">boulevard</a> (today's <i>Bulevar oslobođenja</i>) was cut through the old housings in 1962-1964, establishing major communication lines. Several more boulevards were subsequently built in a similar manner, creating an <a href="/wiki/Orthogonality" title="Orthogonality">orthogonal</a> network over what used to be mostly radial structure of the old town. Those interventions paved the way for a relatively unhampered growth of the city, which almost tripled its population since the 1950s, and <a href="/wiki/Traffic_congestion" title="Traffic congestion">traffic congestions</a> (except on a few critical points) are still relatively mild despite the huge boost of car numbers, especially in later years.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Petrovaradin_Fortress_(Petrovaradinska_tvr%C4%91ava,_P%C3%A9terv%C3%A1radi_v%C3%A1r,_Peterwardein)_by_Pudelek_02_-_clock_tower.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2482" data-file-width="1785" height="306" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Petrovaradin_Fortress_%28Petrovaradinska_tvr%C4%91ava%2C_P%C3%A9terv%C3%A1radi_v%C3%A1r%2C_Peterwardein%29_by_Pudelek_02_-_clock_tower.JPG/220px-Petrovaradin_Fortress_%28Petrovaradinska_tvr%C4%91ava%2C_P%C3%A9terv%C3%A1radi_v%C3%A1r%2C_Peterwardein%29_by_Pudelek_02_-_clock_tower.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Petrovaradin_Fortress_%28Petrovaradinska_tvr%C4%91ava%2C_P%C3%A9terv%C3%A1radi_v%C3%A1r%2C_Peterwardein%29_by_Pudelek_02_-_clock_tower.JPG/330px-Petrovaradin_Fortress_%28Petrovaradinska_tvr%C4%91ava%2C_P%C3%A9terv%C3%A1radi_v%C3%A1r%2C_Peterwardein%29_by_Pudelek_02_-_clock_tower.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Petrovaradin_Fortress_%28Petrovaradinska_tvr%C4%91ava%2C_P%C3%A9terv%C3%A1radi_v%C3%A1r%2C_Peterwardein%29_by_Pudelek_02_-_clock_tower.JPG/440px-Petrovaradin_Fortress_%28Petrovaradinska_tvr%C4%91ava%2C_P%C3%A9terv%C3%A1radi_v%C3%A1r%2C_Peterwardein%29_by_Pudelek_02_-_clock_tower.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Petrovaradin_Fortress_(Petrovaradinska_tvr%C4%91ava,_P%C3%A9terv%C3%A1radi_v%C3%A1r,_Peterwardein)_by_Pudelek_02_-_clock_tower.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Petrovaradin fortress clock tower</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Neighbourhoods">Neighbourhoods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Neighbourhoods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neighborhoods_of_Novi_Sad" title="Neighborhoods of Novi Sad">Neighborhoods of Novi Sad</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Famous_buildings_in_Novi_Sad" title="Famous buildings in Novi Sad">Famous buildings in Novi Sad</a></div>
<p>Some of the oldest neighbourhoods in the city are <a href="/wiki/Stari_Grad,_Novi_Sad" title="Stari Grad, Novi Sad">Stari Grad</a> (Old Town), <a href="/wiki/Rotkvarija_(%C5%BDitni_Trg)" title="Rotkvarija (Žitni Trg)">Rotkvarija</a>, <a href="/wiki/Podbara" title="Podbara">Podbara</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salajka" title="Salajka">Salajka</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sremska_Kamenica" title="Sremska Kamenica">Sremska Kamenica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Petrovaradin" title="Petrovaradin">Petrovaradin</a>, on the right bank of the Danube, were separate towns in the past, but today are parts of the urban area of Novi Sad. <a href="/wiki/Liman,_Novi_Sad" title="Liman, Novi Sad">Liman</a> (divided into four parts, numbered I-IV), as well as <a href="/wiki/Bistrica_(Novo_Naselje)" title="Bistrica (Novo Naselje)">Novo Naselje</a> are neighbourhoods built during the 1960s, 1970s and 1980s with modern buildings and wide boulevards.</p>
<p>New neighbourhoods, like <a href="/wiki/Liman,_Novi_Sad" title="Liman, Novi Sad">Liman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Detelinara" title="Detelinara">Detelinara</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bistrica_(Novo_Naselje)" title="Bistrica (Novo Naselje)">Novo Naselje</a>, with modern high residential buildings emerged from fields and forests surrounding the city to house the huge influx of people from the countryside following World War II. Many old houses in the city centre, <a href="/wiki/Rotkvarija_(%C5%BDitni_Trg)" title="Rotkvarija (Žitni Trg)">Rotkvarija</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bulevar" title="Bulevar">Bulevar</a> neighbourhoods were torn down in the 1950s and 1960s to be replaced with multi-story buildings, as the city experienced a major construction boom during the last 10 years; some neighbourhoods, like <a href="/wiki/Grbavica_(Novi_Sad)" title="Grbavica (Novi Sad)">Grbavica</a> have completely changed their face.</p>
<p>Neighbourhoods with individual housing are mostly located away from the city center; <a href="/wiki/Telep" title="Telep">Telep</a> in the southwest and <a href="/wiki/Klisa,_Serbia" title="Klisa, Serbia">Klisa</a> on the north are the oldest such quarters, while <a href="/wiki/Adice" title="Adice">Adice</a> and <a href="/wiki/Veternik" title="Veternik">Veternik</a> on the west significantly expanded during last 15 years, partly due to an influx of Serb refugees during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yugoslav_wars" title="Yugoslav wars">Yugoslav wars</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Suburbs_and_villages">Suburbs and villages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Suburbs and villages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Besides the urban part of the city (which includes Novi Sad proper, with population of around 250,000, <a href="/wiki/Petrovaradin" title="Petrovaradin">Petrovaradin</a> (around 15,000) and <a href="/wiki/Sremska_Kamenica" title="Sremska Kamenica">Sremska Kamenica</a> (around 12,000), there are 12 more settlements and 1 town in Novi Sad's municipal area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Census_1-4"><a href="#cite_note-Census-1">[1]</a></sup> Some 23.7% of total city's population live in suburbs, the largest being <a href="/wiki/Futog" title="Futog">Futog</a> (20,000), and <a href="/wiki/Veternik" title="Veternik">Veternik</a> (17,000) to the west, which over the years, especially in the 1990s, have grown and physically merged to the city.</p>
<p>The most isolated and the least populated village in the suburban area is <a href="/wiki/Stari_Ledinci" title="Stari Ledinci">Stari Ledinci</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ledinci" title="Ledinci">Ledinci</a>, Stari Ledinci and <a href="/wiki/Bukovac" title="Bukovac">Bukovac</a> are located on <a href="/wiki/Fru%C5%A1ka_Gora" title="Fruška Gora">Fruška Gora</a> slopes and the last two have only one paved road, which connect them to other places. Besides the urban area of Novi Sad, the suburb of Futog is also officially classified as "<i>urban settlement</i>" (a town), while other suburbs are mostly "<i>rural</i>" (villages).</p>
<p>Towns and villages in adjacent municipalities of <a href="/wiki/Sremski_Karlovci" title="Sremski Karlovci">Sremski Karlovci</a>, <a href="/wiki/Temerin" title="Temerin">Temerin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beo%C4%8Din" title="Beočin">Beočin</a>, share the same <a href="/wiki/Public_transport" title="Public transport">public transportation</a> and are economically connected with Novi Sad.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Novi_sad_quarters.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2185" data-file-width="1800" height="364" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Novi_sad_quarters.png/300px-Novi_sad_quarters.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Novi_sad_quarters.png/450px-Novi_sad_quarters.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Novi_sad_quarters.png/600px-Novi_sad_quarters.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Novi_sad_quarters.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Novi Sad is divided into two urban municipalities: Novi Sad proper and Petrovaradin</div>
</div>

<p>Novi Sad is the second largest city in Serbia (after <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>), and the largest city in <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a>. Since its founding, the population of the city has been constantly increasing. According to the 1991 census, 56.2% of the people who came to Novi Sad from 1961 to 1991 were from Vojvodina, while 15.3% came from <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> and 11.7% from rest of Serbia.</p>
<p>In the 1990s and 2000s, the city experienced significant population growth. According to the 2011 census,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-media.popis2011.stat.rs_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-media.popis2011.stat.rs-2">[2]</a></sup> the city's population is 250,439, while in urban area (including adjacent settlements of Petrovaradin, Sremska Kamenica, Veternik and Futog) there are 277,522 inhabitants. Metro area which encompass territory within administrative city limits has 341,625 inhabitants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Census_1-6"><a href="#cite_note-Census-1">[1]</a></sup> According to the information collected by a local <a href="/wiki/Public_service_company" title="Public service company">public service company</a> "Informatika" in 2014, Novi Sad city was inhabited by 270,979 people, while the administrative area was inhabited by 389,784 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Informatika_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Informatika-25">[25]</a></sup></p>

<p>All of the inhabited places in the municipalities have an ethnic Serb majority, while the village of <a href="/wiki/Kisa%C4%8D" title="Kisač">Kisač</a> has an ethnic Slovak majority.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Religious_architecture_in_Novi_Sad" title="Religious architecture in Novi Sad">Religious architecture in Novi Sad</a></div>
<p>According to the 2011 census, the population of the administrative area of Novi Sad (comprising both municipalities) included 270,831 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthodox_Christians" title="Orthodox Christians">Orthodox Christians</a>, 21,530 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholics" title="Catholics">Catholics</a>, 8,499 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestants" title="Protestants">Protestants</a>, 4,760 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a>, 84 <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>, and others. The city is the seat of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serbian_Orthodox" title="Serbian Orthodox">Serbian Orthodox</a> <a href="/wiki/Eparchy_of_Ba%C4%8Dka" title="Eparchy of Bačka">Eparchy of Bačka</a> and of the <a href="/wiki/Muftiship_of_Novi_Sad" title="Muftiship of Novi Sad">Muftiship of Novi Sad</a> of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Islamic_Community_in_Serbia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Islamic Community in Serbia (page does not exist)">Islamic Community in Serbia</a>.</p>
