<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Novi_Sad" title="Politics of Novi Sad">Politics of Novi Sad</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Novi_Sad" title="List of mayors of Novi Sad">List of mayors of Novi Sad</a></div>
<p>Novi Sad is the administrative center of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subdivisions_of_Serbia" title="Subdivisions of Serbia">Autonomous Province</a> of <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a>, and as such, the home to Vojvodina's <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Vojvodina" title="Government of Vojvodina">Government</a> and <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_Vojvodina" title="Assembly of Vojvodina">Provincial Assembly</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RS-NS-NS-P%C3%A9terv%C3%A1rad031.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/RS-NS-NS-P%C3%A9terv%C3%A1rad031.JPG/220px-RS-NS-NS-P%C3%A9terv%C3%A1rad031.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/RS-NS-NS-P%C3%A9terv%C3%A1rad031.JPG/330px-RS-NS-NS-P%C3%A9terv%C3%A1rad031.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/RS-NS-NS-P%C3%A9terv%C3%A1rad031.JPG/440px-RS-NS-NS-P%C3%A9terv%C3%A1rad031.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RS-NS-NS-P%C3%A9terv%C3%A1rad031.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Belgrade Gate</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city's administrative bodies are the city <a href="/wiki/Deliberative_assembly" title="Deliberative assembly">assembly</a> as the representative body, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">mayor</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Local_government" title="Local government">city government</a> as the executive bodies. The members of the city assembly and the mayor are elected by direct elections. The city assembly has 78 seats, while the city government consists of 11 members. The mayor and members of the city's assembly are elected to four-year terms. The city government is elected by the city assembly at the proposal of the mayor.</p>
<p>as of the 2012 election<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the mayor of Novi Sad has been <a href="/wiki/Milo%C5%A1_Vu%C4%8Devi%C4%87" title="Miloš Vučević">Miloš Vučević</a> (<a href="/wiki/Serbian_Progressive_Party" title="Serbian Progressive Party">Serbian Progressive Party</a>); while the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Progressive_Party" title="Serbian Progressive Party">Serbian Progressive Party</a> holds the majority of seats in the city assembly, the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_of_Serbia" title="Socialist Party of Serbia">Socialist Party of Serbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_of_Serbia" title="Democratic Party of Serbia">Democratic Party of Serbia</a> as well as other parties and groups are also represented.</p>
<p>The city of Novi Sad has been divided into 46 <a href="/wiki/List_of_local_communities_in_Novi_Sad" title="List of local communities in Novi Sad">local communities</a> within two urban municipalities, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Novi_Sad_municipality" title="Novi Sad municipality">Novi Sad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Petrovaradin" title="Petrovaradin">Petrovaradin</a>, the border between which is the Danube river.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Coat of arms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the center, there are three towers with eaves encircling their central and top parts. The towers stand separately, the eaves on the roof are cogged, the gates are closed, and the windows are open. The tower in the middle is a bit higher and wider and a white dove flies above it with the olive branch. Below the towers, the wavy stripes represent the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Danube_River" title="Danube River">Danube River</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="City_holidays">City holidays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: City holidays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr>
<td>February 1</td>
<td>On this day, in 1748, Novi Sad gained "free royal city" status.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>October 23</td>
<td>The partisan forces from <a href="/wiki/Syrmia" title="Syrmia">Srem</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ba%C4%8Dka" title="Bačka">Bačka</a> entered and liberated the city from occupation on this day, in 1944.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>November 9</td>
<td>Troops of the Kingdom of Serbia entered the city on this day, in 1918, led by commandant <a href="/wiki/Petar_Bojovi%C4%87" title="Petar Bojović">Petar Bojović</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>November 25</td>
<td>In 1918, the Assembly of <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">Serbs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bunjevci" title="Bunjevci">Bunjevci</a>, and other <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a> of <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a> (<a href="/wiki/Banat,_Ba%C4%8Dka_and_Baranja" title="Banat, Bačka and Baranja">Banat, Bačka and Baranja</a>) in Novi Sad proclaimed the unification of <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a> region with the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia" title="Kingdom of Serbia">Kingdom of Serbia</a>.</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The city also commemorates the year 1694, when it was established.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Master_Centar_-_panoramio.jpg"><img alt="Novi Sad Fair" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Master_Centar_-_panoramio.jpg/200px-Master_Centar_-_panoramio.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Master_Centar_-_panoramio.jpg/300px-Master_Centar_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Master_Centar_-_panoramio.jpg/400px-Master_Centar_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Novi_Sad_Fair" title="Novi Sad Fair">Novi Sad Fair</a> Convention Center</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NISbuildingNS.jpg"><img alt="NIS building" data-file-height="1088" data-file-width="1632" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/NISbuildingNS.jpg/200px-NISbuildingNS.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/NISbuildingNS.jpg/300px-NISbuildingNS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/NISbuildingNS.jpg/400px-NISbuildingNS.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Naftna_Industrija_Srbije" title="Naftna Industrija Srbije">Petroleum Industry of Serbia</a></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Novi Sad is the economic centre of <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a>, the most fertile agricultural region in <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>. The city also is one of the largest economic and cultural centres in Serbia and former <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>.</p>
<p>Novi Sad had always been a relatively developed city within Yugoslavia. In 1981 its GDP per capita was 172% of the Yugoslav average.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> In the 1990s, the city (like the rest of Serbia) was severely affected by an internationally imposed <a href="/wiki/Embargo" title="Embargo">trade embargo</a> and hyperinflation of the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_dinar" title="Yugoslav dinar">Yugoslav dinar</a>. The embargo and economic mismanagement lead to a decay or demise of once big industrial combines, such as <i>Novkabel</i> (electric cable industry), <i>Pobeda</i> (metal industry), <i>Jugoalat</i> (tools), <i>Albus</i> and <i>HINS</i> (chemical industry). Practically the only viable remaining large facility is the oil refinery, located northeast of the town (along with the <a href="/wiki/Thermal_power_station" title="Thermal power station">thermal power plant</a>).</p>
<p>The economy of Novi Sad has mostly recovered from that period and it has grown strongly since 2001, shifting from industry-driven economy to the <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Tertiary sector of the economy">tertiary sector</a>. The processes of <a href="/wiki/Privatization" title="Privatization">privatization</a> of state and society-owned enterprises, as well as strong private incentive, increased the share of privately owned companies to over 95% in the district, and small and medium-size enterprises dominated the city's <a href="/wiki/Economic_development" title="Economic development">economic development</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pkns2_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-pkns2-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>The significance of Novi Sad as a financial centre is proven by numerous banks such as <a href="/wiki/Vojvo%C4%91anska_banka" title="Vojvođanska banka">Vojvođanska Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erste_Bank_Novi_Sad" title="Erste Bank Novi Sad">Erste Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cr%C3%A9dit_Agricole_Srbija" title="Crédit Agricole Srbija">Crédit Agricole</a>, and <a href="/wiki/OTP_banka_Srbija" title="OTP banka Srbija">OTP bank</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> and third largest <a href="/wiki/Insurance" title="Insurance">insurance company</a> in Serbia - <a href="/wiki/DDOR_Novi_Sad" title="DDOR Novi Sad">DDOR Novi Sad</a>. The city is also home to the major energy companies - <a href="/wiki/Naftna_Industrija_Srbije" title="Naftna Industrija Srbije">Naftna Industrija Srbije</a> oil company and <a href="/wiki/Srbijagas" title="Srbijagas">Srbijagas</a> gas company. It is also the seat of the wheat <a href="/wiki/Commodity_market" title="Commodity market">market</a>.</p>
<p>Novi Sad is also a growing <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">information technology</a> center in Serbia second only to <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Novi_Sad,_font%C3%A1na_a_Dunajsk%C3%A1_ulice.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4770" data-file-width="3178" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Novi_Sad%2C_font%C3%A1na_a_Dunajsk%C3%A1_ulice.jpg/220px-Novi_Sad%2C_font%C3%A1na_a_Dunajsk%C3%A1_ulice.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Novi_Sad%2C_font%C3%A1na_a_Dunajsk%C3%A1_ulice.jpg/330px-Novi_Sad%2C_font%C3%A1na_a_Dunajsk%C3%A1_ulice.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Novi_Sad%2C_font%C3%A1na_a_Dunajsk%C3%A1_ulice.jpg/440px-Novi_Sad%2C_font%C3%A1na_a_Dunajsk%C3%A1_ulice.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Novi_Sad,_font%C3%A1na_a_Dunajsk%C3%A1_ulice.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dunavska shopping street</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A3%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B7_%D1%83_%D0%B7%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%83.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/%D0%A3%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B7_%D1%83_%D0%B7%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%83.JPG/200px-%D0%A3%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B7_%D1%83_%D0%B7%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%83.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/%D0%A3%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B7_%D1%83_%D0%B7%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%83.JPG/300px-%D0%A3%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B7_%D1%83_%D0%B7%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%83.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/%D0%A3%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B7_%D1%83_%D0%B7%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%83.JPG/400px-%D0%A3%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B7_%D1%83_%D0%B7%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%83.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A3%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B7_%D1%83_%D0%B7%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%83.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Matica_srpska" title="Matica srpska">Matica srpska</a>, is the oldest cultural-scientific institution in Serbia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the 19th century, the city was the capital of <a href="/wiki/Serbian_culture" title="Serbian culture">Serbian culture</a>, earning the nickname <b>Serbian Athens</b>. In that time, almost every Serbian novelist, poet, jurist, and publicist at the end of 19th century and at the beginning of 20th century had lived or worked in Novi Sad some time of his or her career. Among others, these cultural workers include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vuk_Stefanovi%C4%87_Karad%C5%BEi%C4%87" title="Vuk Stefanović Karadžić">Vuk Stefanović Karadžić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mika_Anti%C4%87" title="Mika Antić">Mika Antić</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C4%90ura_Jak%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Đura Jakšić">Đura Jakšić</a>, etc. <a href="/wiki/Matica_srpska" title="Matica srpska">Matica srpska</a>, the oldest cultural-scientific institution of Serbia, was moved from <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a> to Novi Sad in 1864, and contains second-largest library in the country (the Library of Matica srpska) with over 3.5 million volumes. The <a href="/wiki/Serbian_National_Theatre" title="Serbian National Theatre">Serbian National Theatre</a>, the oldest professional theatre among the <a href="/wiki/South_Slavs" title="South Slavs">South Slavs</a>, was founded in Novi Sad in 1861.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Serbia-0296_-_Serbian_National_Theatre.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Serbia-0296_-_Serbian_National_Theatre.jpg/200px-Serbia-0296_-_Serbian_National_Theatre.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Serbia-0296_-_Serbian_National_Theatre.jpg/300px-Serbia-0296_-_Serbian_National_Theatre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Serbia-0296_-_Serbian_National_Theatre.jpg/400px-Serbia-0296_-_Serbian_National_Theatre.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Serbia-0296_-_Serbian_National_Theatre.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Serbian_National_Theatre" title="Serbian National Theatre">Serbian National Theatre</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Today, Novi Sad is the second cultural centre in <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> (besides <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>) and city's officials try to make the city more attractive to numerous cultural events and music concerts. Since 2000, Novi Sad is home to the <a href="/wiki/Exit_(festival)" title="Exit (festival)">EXIT festival</a>, one of the biggest music summer festival in Europe. Other important cultural events are <a href="/wiki/Sterijino_pozorje" title="Sterijino pozorje">Sterijino pozorje</a> theatre festival, <a href="/wiki/Zmaj_Children_Games" title="Zmaj Children Games">Zmaj Children Games</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Novi_Sad_Literature_Festival" title="International Novi Sad Literature Festival">International Novi Sad Literature Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Novi_Sad_Jazz_Festival" title="Novi Sad Jazz Festival">Novi Sad Jazz Festival</a>, and many others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Besides <a href="/wiki/Serbian_National_Theatre" title="Serbian National Theatre">Serbian National Theatre</a>, the most prominent theatres are also <a href="/wiki/Novi_Sad_Theatre" title="Novi Sad Theatre">Novi Sad Theatre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Youth_Theatre" title="Youth Theatre">Youth Theatre</a>, and Cultural centre of Novi Sad. <a href="/wiki/Novi_Sad_Synagogue" title="Novi Sad Synagogue">Novi Sad Synagogue</a> also houses many cultural events . Other city's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cultural_institutions" title="Cultural institutions">cultural institutions</a> include Detachment of the Serbian Academy of Science and Art, Library of Matica Srpska, Novi Sad City Library and Azbukum. City is also home to the Archive of Vojvodina, which collect many documents from <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a> dating from 1565.</p>
<p>Novi Sad has several folk song societies, which are known as <i>kulturno-umetničko društvo</i> or KUD. The most well known societies in the city are: KUD Svetozar Marković, AKUD Sonja Marinković, SKUD Željezničar, FA Vila and the oldest SZPD <a href="/wiki/NEVEN_Serbian_Craftsmen_Singing_Society" title="NEVEN Serbian Craftsmen Singing Society">Neven</a>, established in 1892.</p>
<p>National minorities expose their own tradition, folklore and songs in Hungarian MKUD Petőfi Sándor, Slovak SKUD Pavel Jozef Šafárik, Ruthenian RKC Novi Sad, and other societies.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%BF%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%81_%D0%BC%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D1%98_%D0%B8_%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%85%D0%B8%D0%B2_%D1%83_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%83.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%BF%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%81_%D0%BC%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D1%98_%D0%B8_%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%85%D0%B8%D0%B2_%D1%83_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%83.JPG/200px-%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%BF%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%81_%D0%BC%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D1%98_%D0%B8_%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%85%D0%B8%D0%B2_%D1%83_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%83.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%BF%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%81_%D0%BC%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D1%98_%D0%B8_%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%85%D0%B8%D0%B2_%D1%83_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%83.JPG/300px-%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%BF%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%81_%D0%BC%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D1%98_%D0%B8_%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%85%D0%B8%D0%B2_%D1%83_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%83.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%BF%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%81_%D0%BC%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D1%98_%D0%B8_%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%85%D0%B8%D0%B2_%D1%83_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%83.JPG/400px-%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%BF%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%81_%D0%BC%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D1%98_%D0%B8_%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%85%D0%B8%D0%B2_%D1%83_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%83.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%BF%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%81_%D0%BC%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D1%98_%D0%B8_%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%85%D0%B8%D0%B2_%D1%83_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%83.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Vojvodina" title="Museum of Vojvodina">Museum of Vojvodina</a> is an <a href="/wiki/Art_museum" title="Art museum">art</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_natural_history_museums" title="List of natural history museums">natural history museum</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city has several museums and galleries, public and privately owned. The most well known museum in the city is <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Vojvodina" title="Museum of Vojvodina">Museum of Vojvodina</a>, founded in 1847, which houses a permanent collection of <a href="/wiki/Serbian_culture" title="Serbian culture">Serbian culture</a> and a life in <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a> through history. Museum of Novi Sad in <a href="/wiki/Petrovaradin_Fortress" title="Petrovaradin Fortress">Petrovaradin Fortress</a> has a permanent collection of history of fortress.</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gallery_of_Matica_Srpska" title="Gallery of Matica Srpska">Gallery of Matica Srpska</a> is the biggest and most respected gallery in the city, which has two galleries in the city centre. There is also <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Gallery_of_Fine_Arts_-_Gift_Collection_of_Rajko_Mamuzi%C4%87" title="The Gallery of Fine Arts - Gift Collection of Rajko Mamuzić">The Gallery of Fine Arts - Gift Collection of Rajko Mamuzić</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Pavle_Beljanski_Memorial_Collection" title="The Pavle Beljanski Memorial Collection">The Pavle Beljanski Memorial Collection</a> - one of the biggest collections of <a href="/wiki/Serbian_art" title="Serbian art">Serbian art</a> from the 1900s until the 1970s.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Novi_Sad" title="Education in Novi Sad">Education in Novi Sad</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gimnazija_Jovan_Jovanovi%C4%87_Zmaj_Novi_Sad.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Gimnazija_Jovan_Jovanovi%C4%87_Zmaj_Novi_Sad.jpg/200px-Gimnazija_Jovan_Jovanovi%C4%87_Zmaj_Novi_Sad.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Gimnazija_Jovan_Jovanovi%C4%87_Zmaj_Novi_Sad.jpg/300px-Gimnazija_Jovan_Jovanovi%C4%87_Zmaj_Novi_Sad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Gimnazija_Jovan_Jovanovi%C4%87_Zmaj_Novi_Sad.jpg/400px-Gimnazija_Jovan_Jovanovi%C4%87_Zmaj_Novi_Sad.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gimnazija_Jovan_Jovanovi%C4%87_Zmaj_Novi_Sad.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_Jovan_Jovanovi%C4%87_Zmaj" title="Gymnasium Jovan Jovanović Zmaj">Gymnasium Jovan Jovanović Zmaj</a> is one of the oldest cultural and educational institutions in Serbia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Novi Sad is one of the most important centers of <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">higher education</a> and research in Serbia, with four universities and numerous professional, technical, and private colleges and <a href="/wiki/Research_institute" title="Research institute">research institutes</a>, including a law school with its own publication.</p>
<p>Novi Sad is home to two universities and seven private faculties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> The largest educational institution in the city is the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Novi_Sad" title="University of Novi Sad">University of Novi Sad</a>, established in 1960. As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, it has with 14 faculties, 9 of which are located in the modern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_campus_in_Novi_Sad" title="University campus in Novi Sad">university campus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uns_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-uns-34">[34]</a></sup> It is attended by more than 50,000 students and has total staff of nearly 5,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uns_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-uns-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are 36 <a href="/wiki/Primary_education" title="Primary education">elementary schools</a> (33 regular and 3 special) with 26,000 students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stat_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-stat-35">[35]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_school" title="High school">secondary school</a> system consists of 11 vocational schools and 4 <a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_(school)" title="Gymnasium (school)">grammar schools</a> with almost 18,000 students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stat_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-stat-35">[35]</a></sup> Other educational institutions include <a href="/wiki/Novi_Sad_Open_University" title="Novi Sad Open University">Novi Sad Open University</a>, offering professional courses in <a href="/wiki/Adult_education" title="Adult education">adult education</a> and <a href="/wiki/Novi_Sad_Theological_College" title="Novi Sad Theological College">Protestant Theological Seminary</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Crowd_at_David_Guetta,_Dance_Arena,_Exit_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="849" data-file-width="1340" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Crowd_at_David_Guetta%2C_Dance_Arena%2C_Exit_2013.jpg/200px-Crowd_at_David_Guetta%2C_Dance_Arena%2C_Exit_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Crowd_at_David_Guetta%2C_Dance_Arena%2C_Exit_2013.jpg/300px-Crowd_at_David_Guetta%2C_Dance_Arena%2C_Exit_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Crowd_at_David_Guetta%2C_Dance_Arena%2C_Exit_2013.jpg/400px-Crowd_at_David_Guetta%2C_Dance_Arena%2C_Exit_2013.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Crowd_at_David_Guetta,_Dance_Arena,_Exit_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Exit_(festival)" title="Exit (festival)">Exit festival</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The number of tourists visiting Novi Sad each year has steadily risen since 2000. Every year, in the beginning of July, during the annual <a href="/wiki/Exit_(festival)" title="Exit (festival)">EXIT music festival</a>, the city is full of young people from all over Europe. In 2008, over 200,000 people visited the festival.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Besides EXIT festival, <a href="/wiki/Novi_Sad_Fair" title="Novi Sad Fair">Novi Sad Fair</a> attracts many <a href="/wiki/Businessperson" title="Businessperson">business people</a> into the city; in May, the city is home to the biggest <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_show" title="Agricultural show">agricultural show</a> in the region, which 600,000 people visited in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> There is also a tourist port near <a href="/wiki/Varadin_Bridge" title="Varadin Bridge">Varadin Bridge</a> in the city centre welcoming various river cruise vessels from across Europe who cruise on Danube river.</p>
<p>The most recognized structure in Novi Sad is <a href="/wiki/Petrovaradin_Fortress" title="Petrovaradin Fortress">Petrovaradin Fortress</a>, which dominates the city and with scenic views of the city. Besides the fortress, there is also historic neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Stari_Grad,_Novi_Sad" title="Stari Grad, Novi Sad">Stari Grad</a>, with many monuments, museums, caffes, restaurants and shops. There is also a <a href="/wiki/Fru%C5%A1ka_Gora" title="Fruška Gora">National Park of Fruška Gora</a> nearby, approx. 20 km (12 mi) from city centre.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Novi Sad has one major daily newspaper, <i><a href="/wiki/Dnevnik_(Novi_Sad)" title="Dnevnik (Novi Sad)">Dnevnik</a></i>, and among the periodicals monthly magazine <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Vojvodjanski_magazin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Vojvodjanski magazin (page does not exist)">Vojvodjanski magazin</a></i> stands out. The city is home to the main headquarters of the regional <a href="/wiki/Public_broadcasting" title="Public broadcasting">public broadcaster</a> <a href="/wiki/Radio_Television_of_Vojvodina" title="Radio Television of Vojvodina">Radio Television of Vojvodina</a> – RTV and city's public broadcaster Novosadska televizija,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> as well as a few commercial TV stations: Kanal 9,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Panonija<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> and RTV Most.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Major local commercial radio stations are <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Radio_AS&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Radio AS (page does not exist)">Radio AS</a> FM and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Radio_021&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Radio 021 (page does not exist)">Radio 021</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>Novi Sad is also known as a center of publishing. The most prominent publishers are Matica srpska, Stilos and Prometej. Well-known journals in literature and art are <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Letopis_Matice_srpske" title="Letopis Matice srpske">Letopis Matice srpske</a></i>, the oldest Serbian Journal; <i>Polja</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> issued by the <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Center_of_Novi_Sad" title="Cultural Center of Novi Sad">Cultural Center of Novi Sad</a> and <i>Zlatna greda</i> by the Association of Writers of Vojvodina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spens.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="704" data-file-width="1024" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Spens.jpg/200px-Spens.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Spens.jpg/300px-Spens.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Spens.jpg/400px-Spens.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spens.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spens_Sports_Center" title="Spens Sports Center">Spens Sports Center</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Sports started to develop in 1790 with the foundation of <i>"City Marksmen Association"</i>. However, its serious development started after the establishment of the <i>Municipal Association of Physical Culture</i> in 1959 and after 1981, when <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spens_Sports_Center" title="Spens Sports Center">Spens Sports Center</a> was built. Today, about 220 sports organizations are active in Novi Sad.</p>
<p>Professional sport in Novi Sad revolves around <a href="/wiki/SD_Vojvodina" title="SD Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a> multi-sport club. <a href="/wiki/FK_Vojvodina" title="FK Vojvodina">FK Vojvodina</a> football club is 3rd all-time best football club in Serbia, behind Belgrade rivals of <a href="/wiki/Red_Star_Belgrade" title="Red Star Belgrade">Red Star</a> and <a href="/wiki/FK_Partizan" title="FK Partizan">Partizan</a>, having won 2 championships (1966 and 1989, respectively). <a href="/wiki/OK_Vojvodina" title="OK Vojvodina">OK Vojvodina</a> is most successful volleyball club in the country with 13 championship titles. <a href="/wiki/RK_Vojvodina" title="RK Vojvodina">RK Vojvodina</a> handball club are current national champions.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2009_European_Athletics_Junior_Championships.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/2009_European_Athletics_Junior_Championships.JPG/200px-2009_European_Athletics_Junior_Championships.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/2009_European_Athletics_Junior_Championships.JPG/300px-2009_European_Athletics_Junior_Championships.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/2009_European_Athletics_Junior_Championships.JPG/400px-2009_European_Athletics_Junior_Championships.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2009_European_Athletics_Junior_Championships.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Kara%C4%91or%C4%91e_Stadium" title="Karađorđe Stadium">Karađorđe Stadium</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Citizens of Novi Sad participated in the first <a href="/wiki/1896_Summer_Olympics" title="1896 Summer Olympics">Olympic Games</a> in <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>. The largest number of sportsmen from Novi Sad participated in the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia_at_the_1996_Summer_Olympics" title="Yugoslavia at the 1996 Summer Olympics">Atlanta Olympic Games</a> – 11, and they won 6 medals, while in <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia_at_the_1980_Summer_Olympics" title="Yugoslavia at the 1980 Summer Olympics">Moscow</a> – 3, and in <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia_at_the_1976_Summer_Olympics" title="Yugoslavia at the 1976 Summer Olympics">Montreal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia_at_the_1956_Summer_Olympics" title="Yugoslavia at the 1956 Summer Olympics">Melbourne</a> – 2.</p>
<p>Novi Sad was the host of the European and World Championships in <a href="/wiki/Table_tennis" title="Table tennis">table tennis</a> in 1981,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.D0.9D.D0.B0.D1.98.D0.B7.D0.BD.D0.B0.D1.87.D0.B0.D1.98.D0.BD.D0.B8.D1.98.D0.B5_.D0.BF.D1.80.D0.B8.D1.80.D0.B5.D0.B4.D0.B1.D0.B5_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-.D0.9D.D0.B0.D1.98.D0.B7.D0.BD.D0.B0.D1.87.D0.B0.D1.98.D0.BD.D0.B8.D1.98.D0.B5_.D0.BF.D1.80.D0.B8.D1.80.D0.B5.D0.B4.D0.B1.D0.B5-45">[45]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chess_Olympiad" title="Chess Olympiad">29th Chess Olympiad</a> in 1990, European and World Championships in <a href="/wiki/Sambo_(martial_art)" title="Sambo (martial art)">sambo</a>, Balkan and European Championships in <a href="/wiki/Judo" title="Judo">judo</a>, 1987 final match in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saporta_Cup" title="Saporta Cup">Cup Winners Cup</a> of European <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">Basketball</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.D0.9D.D0.B0.D1.98.D0.B7.D0.BD.D0.B0.D1.87.D0.B0.D1.98.D0.BD.D0.B8.D1.98.D0.B5_.D0.BF.D1.80.D0.B8.D1.80.D0.B5.D0.B4.D0.B1.D0.B5_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-.D0.9D.D0.B0.D1.98.D0.B7.D0.BD.D0.B0.D1.87.D0.B0.D1.98.D0.BD.D0.B8.D1.98.D0.B5_.D0.BF.D1.80.D0.B8.D1.80.D0.B5.D0.B4.D0.B1.D0.B5-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cup_Winners.E2.80.99_Cup_1986-87_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cup_Winners.E2.80.99_Cup_1986-87-46">[46]</a></sup> and final tournament of the European Cup in <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.D0.9D.D0.B0.D1.98.D0.B7.D0.BD.D0.B0.D1.87.D0.B0.D1.98.D0.BD.D0.B8.D1.98.D0.B5_.D0.BF.D1.80.D0.B8.D1.80.D0.B5.D0.B4.D0.B1.D0.B5_45-2"><a href="#cite_note-.D0.9D.D0.B0.D1.98.D0.B7.D0.BD.D0.B0.D1.87.D0.B0.D1.98.D0.BD.D0.B8.D1.98.D0.B5_.D0.BF.D1.80.D0.B8.D1.80.D0.B5.D0.B4.D0.B1.D0.B5-45">[45]</a></sup> Apart from that Novi Sad is the host of the World League in volleyball and traditional sport events such as Novi Sad marathon, international swimming rally and many other events. Between the 16 and 20 September 2005, Novi Sad co-hosted the <a href="/wiki/EuroBasket_2005" title="EuroBasket 2005">2005 European Basketball Championship</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.D0.9D.D0.B0.D1.98.D0.B7.D0.BD.D0.B0.D1.87.D0.B0.D1.98.D0.BD.D0.B8.D1.98.D0.B5_.D0.BF.D1.80.D0.B8.D1.80.D0.B5.D0.B4.D0.B1.D0.B5_45-3"><a href="#cite_note-.D0.9D.D0.B0.D1.98.D0.B7.D0.BD.D0.B0.D1.87.D0.B0.D1.98.D0.BD.D0.B8.D1.98.D0.B5_.D0.BF.D1.80.D0.B8.D1.80.D0.B5.D0.B4.D0.B1.D0.B5-45">[45]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recreation">Recreation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Recreation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Odmaraliste_Zmajevac_na_Fruskoj_Gori.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3072" data-file-width="4608" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Odmaraliste_Zmajevac_na_Fruskoj_Gori.jpg/220px-Odmaraliste_Zmajevac_na_Fruskoj_Gori.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Odmaraliste_Zmajevac_na_Fruskoj_Gori.jpg/330px-Odmaraliste_Zmajevac_na_Fruskoj_Gori.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Odmaraliste_Zmajevac_na_Fruskoj_Gori.jpg/440px-Odmaraliste_Zmajevac_na_Fruskoj_Gori.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Odmaraliste_Zmajevac_na_Fruskoj_Gori.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Fru%C5%A1ka_Gora" title="Fruška Gora">Fruška Gora National Park</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Apart from the culture of attending sports events, people from Novi Sad participate in a wide range of recreational and leisure activities. <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> and <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> are the most popular participation <a href="/wiki/Team_sport" title="Team sport">team sports</a> in Novi Sad. Cycling is also very popular in Novi Sad. Novi Sad's flat terrain and extensive off-road paths in the mountainous part of town, in <a href="/wiki/Fru%C5%A1ka_Gora" title="Fruška Gora">Fruška Gora</a> is conducive to riding. Hundreds of commuters cycle the roads, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Segregated_cycle_facilities" title="Segregated cycle facilities">bike lanes and bike paths</a> daily.</p>
<p>Proximity to the <a href="/wiki/Fru%C5%A1ka_Gora" title="Fruška Gora">Fruška Gora National Park</a> attracts many people from the city on weekends in many hiking trails, restaurants and monasteries on the mountain. In the first weekend of May, there is a "<i><a href="/wiki/Fru%C5%A1kogorski_maraton" title="Fruškogorski maraton">Fruška Gora Marathon</a></i>", with many hiking trails for hikers, runners and cyclists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> During the summer, there is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lake_of_Ledinci" title="Lake of Ledinci">Lake of Ledinci</a> in Fruška Gora, but also there are numerous beaches on the Danube, the largest being <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0trand" title="Štrand">Štrand</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Liman,_Novi_Sad" title="Liman, Novi Sad">Liman</a> neighborhood. There are also a couple of small recreational marinas on the river.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure_of_Novi_Sad" title="Infrastructure of Novi Sad">Infrastructure of Novi Sad</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B0_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8-%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%B4.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2304" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B0_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8-%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%B4.jpg/220px-%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B0_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8-%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%B4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B0_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8-%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%B4.jpg/330px-%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B0_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8-%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%B4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B0_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8-%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%B4.jpg/440px-%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B0_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8-%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%B4.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

<div class="thumbcaption">

<a href="/wiki/Liberty_Bridge,_Novi_Sad" title="Liberty Bridge, Novi Sad">Liberty Bridge</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Novi Sad lies on the branch B of <a href="/wiki/Pan-European_Corridor_X" title="Pan-European Corridor X">Pan-European Corridor X</a>. <a href="/wiki/A1_motorway_(Serbia)" title="A1 motorway (Serbia)">A1 motorway</a> connects the city with <a href="/wiki/Subotica" title="Subotica">Subotica</a> on north and <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> on south. It is concurrent with Budapest–Belgrade railroad, which connects it to major European cities. Novi Sad is connected with <a href="/wiki/Zrenjanin" title="Zrenjanin">Zrenjanin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timi%C8%99oara" title="Timișoara">Timișoara</a> on the northwest and <a href="/wiki/Ruma" title="Ruma">Ruma</a> on south with a regional highway; there are long-term plans to upgrade it to a motorway or an expressway, with a tunnel under the <a href="/wiki/Fru%C5%A1ka_Gora" title="Fruška Gora">Fruška Gora</a> shortcutting the <i>Iriški Venac</i> mountain pass.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>Novi Sad currently does not have its own civil airport. The city is about a one-hour drive from <a href="/wiki/Belgrade_Nikola_Tesla_Airport" title="Belgrade Nikola Tesla Airport">Belgrade Nikola Tesla Airport</a>, which connects it with capitals across Europe. Small <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C4%8Cenej_Airport" title="Čenej Airport">Čenej Airport</a> north of the city is used for sport and agricultural purposes. There are plans to upgrade it to serve for cargo and small-scale public transport,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> but the future of this initiative is uncertain.</p>
<p>Three bridges cross the Danube in Novi Sad: Liberty Bridge (Most Slobode) connects <a href="/wiki/Sremska_Kamenica" title="Sremska Kamenica">Sremska Kamenica</a> with the city proper. <a href="/wiki/Varadin_Bridge" title="Varadin Bridge">Varadin Bridge</a> (Varadinski most), connects Petrovaradin with city centre, along with the temporary <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Road-Railway_Bridge" title="Road-Railway Bridge">Road-Railway Bridge</a>, used chiefly for railway and heavy truck traffic. Its replacement with the new Žeželj Bridge is currently under construction and will be opened to traffic in 2017. Four bridges span the Danube-Tisa-Danube canal, running north of the city center.</p>
<p>The main public transportation system in Novi Sad consists of <a href="/wiki/Bus" title="Bus">bus lines</a>. There are twenty-one urban lines and twenty-nine suburban lines. The operator is <a href="/wiki/JGSP_Novi_Sad" title="JGSP Novi Sad">JGSP Novi Sad</a>, with its main bus station at the northern end of the <a href="/wiki/Bulevar" title="Bulevar">Liberation Boulevard</a>, next to the railway station. In addition, there are numerous taxi companies serving the city. The city used to have <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Novi_Sad_tram_system" title="Novi Sad tram system">a tram system</a>, but it was disassembled in 1958.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_cooperation">International cooperation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: International cooperation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Serbia" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Serbia">List of twin towns and sister cities in Serbia</a></div>
<p>Novi Sad has relationships with several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Town_twinning" title="Town twinning">twin</a> towns. One of the main streets in its <a href="/wiki/Stari_Grad,_Novi_Sad" title="Stari Grad, Novi Sad">city centre</a> is named after <a href="/wiki/Modena" title="Modena">Modena</a> in <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>; and likewise Modena has named a park in its town centre Parco di Piazza d'Armi Novi Sad. The <a href="/wiki/River_Wensum" title="River Wensum">Novi Sad Friendship Bridge</a> in <a href="/wiki/Norwich" title="Norwich">Norwich</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buro_Happold" title="Buro Happold">Buro Happold</a>, was also named in honour of Novi Sad. Besides twin cities, Novi Sad has many signed agreements on joint cooperation with many European cities (<i>see also: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Novi_Sad#Twin_cities" title="Politics of Novi Sad">Twin cities of Novi Sad</a></i>). Novi Sad's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Town_twinning" title="Town twinning">twin towns</a> are:</p>

<p>Novi Sad is an associated member of <a href="/wiki/Eurocities" title="Eurocities">Eurocities</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Novi_Sad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>

<td colspan="2"></td>

<tr>
<td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="3">
<div><sup><small>1</small></sup> <span class="wrap"><a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> is the subject of a territorial dispute between the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Republic of Kosovo</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Republic of Serbia</a>. The Republic of Kosovo <a href="/wiki/2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" title="2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">unilaterally declared independence</a> on 17 February 2008, but <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serbia%27s_reaction_to_the_2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" title="Serbia's reaction to the 2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">Serbia continues to claim</a> it as part of its <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo_and_Metohija" title="Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija">own sovereign territory</a>. The two governments <a href="/wiki/Belgrade%E2%80%93Pristina_negotiations" title="Belgrade–Pristina negotiations">began to normalise relations</a> in 2013, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Agreement_(2013)" title="Brussels Agreement (2013)">Brussels Agreement</a>. Kosovo has received recognition as an independent state from <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">110</a> out of 193 <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">member states</a>.</span></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
</td>
